# Advanced Spline Shapes | ezEdits Wiki

The following `//ezspline` subcommands feature three very powerful but more complex spline shapes with effectively limitless customizability.

* * *

#### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#undefined)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-8dc651a532af9c52e91f3caa844f52df898ad3b3%252FSplinesNoise.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f5126d1&sv=2)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#noise)

`//ezspline` `noise`

Noise Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#noise-spline)

`**//ezsp noise**` `**<palette>**` [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 `**[noise]**` `**[depth]**` [`**[-s <stretch>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#stretch-s-less-than-stretchfactor-greater-than)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a noise-based spline along the selected positions.

*   `**<Palette>**`:
    
    *   Specifies the blocks that the spline should be made out of.
        
    
*   `**[noise]**` (Default: "Perlin(Freq:2,z:0.5)"):
    
    *   The noise that should be embedded along the spline path.
        
    
*   `**[depth]**` (Default: 0.7):
    
    *   How deep the noise should cut into the cylinder-shaped spline. Depths approaching 0 approach the original cylinder-shaped spline, 0.5 means the noise may reach half the radius deep, and 1.0 means the full radius, reaching the center. Larger than 1.0 will result in a choppy look.
        
    
*   `**[-i <expression>]**` (Default: "`r=sqrt(x*x+y*y);t=(r-1)/d+1;f=r>1?1:(4*r*(r-1))^2;g=f*t+(1-f)*n;p=max((r-1)/min(d,1)+1,.001);(g>t)*p`"):
    
    *   Advanced parameter for nerds. Ignore if this above looks scary.
        
    *   This expression implements the functionality of the noise cutting into a cylinder at a certain relative `<depth>`. [Derivation](https://www.desmos.com/calculator/qw8fro1npf)
        . If you _**really**_ want to, you can come up with a different expression here to get a different result. If you don't need custom noises just use `//ezspline expression` instead though.
        
    *   Input parameters are `_x,y,z,n,d_` whereby `_x,y,z_` are assigned like in [//ezspline expression](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#expression-spline)
        , `_n_` is the evaluation of the given `<noise>` at the coordinates `_x,y,z_` and `_d_` is the given `<depth>` parameter.
        
    *   An alternative expression could be:
        
        *   `r=sqrt(x*x+y*y);(r<1&&n>0.5)*max(n,0.01)`: If you only want the noise to be restricted to a cylinder shape
            
        
    

_The remaining arguments are outlined on the_ [_Common Parameters_](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters)
 _subpage._

Example:

`//ezspline noise ##Grayscale 10`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-8dc651a532af9c52e91f3caa844f52df898ad3b3%252FSplinesNoise.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f5126d1&sv=2)

Demos[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#demos)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-f72ef870ea4b052a156e04309976dfb89a545942%252FSplinesNoise_example2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3e6cc11d&sv=2)

Just a small, quick set of noise commands I threw together to show what the noise spline can do. ~eztaK

`//ezspline noise -##Magma 5,25 Ce(F:1.5,fO:1,cR:sub,M:OR,U:-.6) 0.6 -t 90`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-995d85521b9421c4660d7aaf6b14c9d5f719d0ab%252FSplinesNoise_example3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3cd3d967&sv=2)

`//ezspline noise ##GrayWarm(3:11),251:8*15 25,10,25 Ce(F:1.6,fO:1,cD:r,cR:r,M:OR,L:-1.1,U:-.2) 0.4`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-5ecae0c223c8caa223df719a65fc9b61eb6e08b8%252FSplinesNoise_example4.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2ed1344c&sv=2)

`//ezspline noise -w Panes light_gray_stained_glass 20,15,25 Ce(f:1.4,z:.3,m:or,l:-1,u:-0.5) 3 -t 600 -i t=0.2;r=sqrt(x*x+y*y);m=1-abs(2*r-t-1)/abs(t-1);n<m&&r<1`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-26e84ab35988367d8741df459985c67f941cabc4%252FSplinesNoise_example5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=290cd687&sv=2)

`//ezspline noise ##Brown 20,12 Ce(f:4,cr:sub,cj:.8,m:or,u:-.5,l:-1.3) 0.2 -s 6 -t 20`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-bef535c4de7df38e54733c54eac40af7185591a8%252FSplinesNoise_example6.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=aa731dd6&sv=2)

`//ezspline noise -##GlowBlue(6:16) 20,12 Ce(f:2,cr:sub,m:or,u:-.55,l:-0.551,z:0.1) 0.9 -t 200`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-e8ae35d44a85937199170571c145569af27c38e5%252FSplinesNoise_example7.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=49a59ae0&sv=2)

`//ezspline noise -w Slabs ##GrayCold(4:11),waxed_weathered_cut_copper 20 Ce(f:1.5,cr:sub,m:or,u:-0.85,l:-.5,y:0.3) -n UPRIGHT -i (x*x+n+y*y<1&&y<0)*(y+0.97)`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-685c4e8e6f22519c2865dc80c26af625a3388b31%252FSplinesNoise_example8.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fca7ae60&sv=2)

* * *

#### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#undefined-1)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-363f2a6d16839c7d3d0509d9b1d3b6a315954414%252FSplinesExpression.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ee0de9f6&sv=2)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#expression)

`//ezspline` `expression`

Expression Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#expression-spline)

`**//ezsp expression**` `<palette>` [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
[`**[-s <stretch>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#stretch-s-less-than-stretchfactor-greater-than)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 `**[-z] [-o]**` [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)
 `**<expression...>**`

Generates a spline shaped by the given WorldEdit expression along the selected positions.

*   `**<Palette>**`:
    
    *   Specifies the block palette.
        
    
*   `**[-z]**`:
    
    *   Without setting this flag, the domain of the z-axis is 0 to the length of the spline divided by the radius. You may set this flag to normalize the z-Axis, that runs along the path of the spline, to the \[-1,1\] domain.
        
    
*   `**[-o]**`:
    
    *   By default, expression output maps >0..1 to the palette. Use this flag to instead map the output to whole numbers.
        
    
*   `**<expression...>**`:
    
    *   [A WorldEdit expression](https://worldedit.enginehub.org/en/latest/usage/other/expressions/)
        . Input variables are
        
        *   \-1 ≤ `_x_` ≤ 1
            
        *   \-1 ≤ `_y_` ≤ 1
            
        *   0 ≤ `_z_` ≤ L, whereby L is the length of the spline divided by its radius.
            
        *   or -1 ≤ `_z_` ≤ 1, if you're using the `-z` flag.
            
        
    *   Output is either a normalized palette index (0,1\] or if using the -o flag (0,P\] whereby P is the number of blocks in the palette. Note that <=0 means not placing any block.
        
    

_The remaining arguments are outlined on the_ [_Common Parameters_](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters)
 _subpage._

Example:

`//ezspline expression clay 10 -t 90 R=0.2;r=0.1;w=0.7;s=0.5;sqrt((abs(x)-w)^2+y^2)<R||sqrt(((z+1)%s-r)^2+y^2)<r&&abs(x)<w`

Expression by [imhols](https://twitter.com/imhols1)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-363f2a6d16839c7d3d0509d9b1d3b6a315954414%252FSplinesExpression.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ee0de9f6&sv=2)

* * *

#### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#undefined-2)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-f247eeda9d9eb1ec93f41fce66c38c6aa2b8e916%252FSplinesStructure_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a7ab0825&sv=2)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#structure)

`//ezspline` `structure`

Structure Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/advanced-spline-shapes#structure-spline)

`**//ezsp structure**` `**<structure>**` [`**[radii]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
[`**[-s <stretch>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#stretch-s-less-than-stretchfactor-greater-than)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 `**[-z]**` [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Embeds a structure along the path defined by the selected convex region.

*   `**<structure>**`:
    
    *   The shape/clipboard/schematic to embed along the path. See [Available Structures](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/available-structures)
        .
        
    
*   `**[-z]**`:
    
    *   Normalizes the Z-Axis, which results in exactly one structure being stretched out throughout the entire length of the path.
        
    

The structure will be placed in its Z-direction facing along the path. Multiple instances will be repeated one after another as often as its bounding box fits, unless you use `-z`, in which case one instance of the structure will be stretched across the whole length of the path.

Specifically for `//ezsp structure`, if the [`[radii]`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 argument is left out, we will automatically calculate the radius at which the structure is generated at its original/inherent size.

_The remaining arguments are outlined on the_ [_Common Parameters_](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters)
 _subpage._

**Examples**:

`//ezsp structure TS(P:##GlowPurple,S:Heart,T:=(z+y)*.4+.5) 12`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-f247eeda9d9eb1ec93f41fce66c38c6aa2b8e916%252FSplinesStructure_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a7ab0825&sv=2)

# Primary+Secondary Alignment | ezEdits Wiki

The two alignment directions define the _orientation_ at which the structure is placed.

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#explanation)

Explanation


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Every structure has an intrinsic "up" direction and an intrinsic "forward" direction. By default, structures are placed with their up direction facing, well, up (+y), and with their forward direction facing forward (+x).

The most important thing is that now you can control how a structure is placed by defining where its up direction and where its forward direction should face.

We let the user define the alignment using two directions:

The `<primary>` direction _defines_ the placement's +y direction.

The `<secondary>` direction _implies_ the placement's +x direction. From all directions perpendicular to the primary direction, the chosen +x direction is the one that most closely aligns with the given secondary direction.

Note: The primary and secondary may not be the same direction.

More in-depth explanation using examples:[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#more-in-depth-explanation-using-examples)

Let's say this is our build that we want to place, by for example having it as our current WorldEdit clipboard.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-2df40aa0623d2477e4ecdc2333758516e67a215e%252FAlignmentGuide_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ab461458&sv=2)

For reference, the red beam is facing towards positive x (east), the blue beam is facing towards positive z (south), and the green beam is facing towards positive y (up).

We now want to place it at various orientations using any of the ezEdits structure commands. For this, we may define a `<primary>` and `<secondary>` direction. Let us go through a few examples for a few such assignments of these parameters and try to understand what is happening:

Let's set the `<primary>` to `up` and the `<secondary>` to `east` (You'd use the [Constant](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#constant)
 mode for that.) (These directions are the default directions):

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-2df40aa0623d2477e4ecdc2333758516e67a215e%252FAlignmentGuide_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ab461458&sv=2)

Our shape is pasted exactly in the same orientation as we copied it. Up is still up, right is still right, and so on.

Now, consider the following three examples:

1.  The `**<primary>**` is set to `**south**` and the `<secondary>` remains at `east`:
    

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-ea0234772641afca937910cd4bd493d3294372a2%252FAlignmentGuide_example2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b84e10ef&sv=2)

Notice how, what was originally _"up"_ when we copied it, i.e. the green beam in our case, is pointing into the direction that we set the primary to: _south_. Meanwhile what was originally _east_, is still _east_. The blue beam is going down as a consequence of this 90° rotation.

1.  The `**<primary>**` is set to the vector `**(0,1,1)**`, i.e. the direction going "diagonally" up and south, and the `<secondary>` to `east`:
    

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-562a8ee5f58bf92602cbbdecd3832ac28243f629%252FAlignmentGuide_example3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7bf36878&sv=2)

Notice again, how what was originally _"up"_ when we copied it, i.e. the green beam in our case, is pointing into the direction that we set the primary to: _diagonally up and south_.

1.  The `**<primary>**` is set to the vector `**(1,1,0)**`, i.e. the direction going diagonally up and **east**, while the `<secondary>` is set to `east`:
    

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-c54d162decc5ad4f2f81bb7e19f1a94a071517d1%252FAlignmentGuide_example4.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=505a26fc&sv=2)

The green beam is correctly pointing along the primary direction, diagonally up and east. Whatever was pointing _up_ when we //copy'd our clipboard is always aligned with whatever direction the primary is set to!

But now, even though the secondary is set to _east_, the red beam is not pointing directly east anymore (but diagonally down and east). This is intended behaviour.

Imagine if it were pointing east: Then the green and red beam would be at a 45° angle instead of the original 90° angle. Our structure would be deformed/bent/sheared.

What we decided to implement instead, is that (while we align the structure's +y direction with the given primary direction) instead of aligning the structure's +x direction with the given secondary direction, we choose the direction that is most similar to the given secondary direction but that is still perpendicular to the primary.

So, if the primary and secondary are not perfectly perpendicular, as in the example above, the secondary is swapped out with the most similar but still perpendicular vector!

Just for reference, here's a small GIF that shows the remaining perpendicular secondary directions for a set primary direction:

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-3a3c081aa9c8c4c8a14d9901b242613301ea2854%252FAlignmentGuide_example5.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e24389c&sv=2)

To give a final example:

The `**<primary>**` is set to the vector `**(-1,2,-1)**`, i.e. a direction going up and northwest, while the `**<secondary>**` is set to `**west**`:

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-65c885742c1e22fc8717743ff7fda7c842f59c19%252FAlignmentGuide_example6.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4f7bf05&sv=2)

As you can see, the green beam, or what was originally up in our build when we copied it, is now pointing into our specified `northwest+2*up` direction, while the red beam, or what was originally east when we copied, is now pointing as `west` as it can while still being perpendicular to the primary.

All of this applies independently of your current clipboard. Here's another structure at its original orientation followed by its placement aligned just like the previous example.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-a26b64cdbdef88c9b36c823c75836e76eb39cfbb%252FAlignmentGuide_example7.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8e5feb0e&sv=2)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-b307e97cb93676a5611d2c6ef0112232fc47323e%252FAlignmentGuide_example8.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2d9fca8e&sv=2)

Can you see why setting the primary to `(-1,2-1)` and the secondary to `west` leads to the leaf being oriented like that?

* * *

By the way, the command used was

`//ezbrush place Clipboard Constant(Direction:(-1,2,-1)) Constant(Direction:west)`

or, if you fancy abbreviations,

`//ezbr pl Cl C(D:(-1,2,-1)) C(D:west)`

With this primary + secondary system, we hope that you can easily and quickly construct your desired 3D orientation for each structure placement in any scenario.

* * *

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#overview)

Overview


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The primary and secondary can be set to either:

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#constant)

Name

[`**Constant**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#constant)

Abbreviation

`**C**`

Description

Explicitly set a constant direction for all placements.

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#random)

Name

[`**Random**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#random)

Abbreviation

`**R**`

Description

Random direction for each placement.

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#noise)

Name

[`**Noise**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#noise)

Abbreviation

`**N**`

Description

Direction based on the evaluation of a noise function at the placement's position.

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#aim)

Name

[`**Aim**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#aim)

Abbreviation

`**A**`

Description

Your player aim direction.

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#upward)

Name

[`**Upward**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#upward)

Abbreviation

`**U**`

Description

The most upwards perpendicular direction to your aim.

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#playerrelative)

Name

[`**PlayerRelative**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#playerrelative)

Abbreviation

`**P**`

Description

The direction from the placement's position towards the current player position.

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#surfacenormal)

Name

[`**SurfaceNormal**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#surfacenormal)

Abbreviation

`**S**`

Description

The approximate surface-normal in the region of the placement's position.

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#viewdiff)

Name

[`**ViewDiff**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#viewdiff)

Abbreviation

`**V**`

Description

Define a direction using two clicks. Exclusively for brushes.

Name

[`**Expression**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#expression)

Abbreviation

`**E**`

Description

Define a direction through an expression over each placement position.

* * *

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#settings)

Settings


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#constant)

Constant

Explicitly set a constant direction for all placements.

Syntax: `**Constant**` or `**Constant(Direction:<direction>)**`

Abbreviation: `**C**` or `**C(D:<direction>)**`

If you do not specify a `<direction>`, then:

*   the default direction is **+y** if you're setting the `<primary>`.
    
*   the default direction is **+x** if you're setting the `<secondary>`.
    

There are various ways to define a direction. From using the axes, cardinal directions, vector notation, or player relative directions like forward, left, right, etc. Pro tip: You can also add directions together using simple arithmetic operators, like `east-z+(0,0.5,0)`. Pro tip²: Put `=` at the end to evaluate your direction expression as you are typing it.

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples)

`//ezsc Clipboard C(D:(0,2,0)) C(D:east)`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-5be682f0df9ec79ef131a3b7b9b942b7556f1f9a%252FConstantAlignment_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c55e150e&sv=2)

`//ezsc Clipboard C(D:(-1,2,-1)) C(D:east)`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-7e507616bd64a5a77aa6db7c2391e7dc22539497%252FConstantAlignment_example2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9143c6b2&sv=2)

`//ezsc Clipboard C(D:(-1,2,-1)) C(D:-aim)`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-a1edce5c9ceca554bc1985d3177236a245238e2c%252FConstantAlignment_example3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2639db6c&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#random)

Random

Random direction for each placement.

Syntax: `**Random**`

Abbreviation: `**R**`

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-1)

`//ezsc Clipboard Constant Random`

Only setting the `<secondary>` to Random here, primary remains pointing up. Notice how our structure's up direction (green beam) remains up (primary is set to up), but each placement is randomly rotated around the primary (y-axis in this case) since the secondary is random.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-63836672c16b47429e6350f80b1505580a800aa2%252FRandomAlignment_demo1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2a23973&sv=2)

`//ezsc Clipboard Random Constant`

Only setting the `<primary>` to Random, secondary remains pointing east. The terrain was replaced with glass so you can see better. Notice how the green beam is now facing all kinds of directions, but the red beam is roughly pointing east for all placements.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-6dd8a8ddf2b068b9f1822495d2e97a3bac47e60e%252FRandomAlignment_demo2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=56b940&sv=2)

`//ezsc Clipboard Random Random`

If we set both to Random, then we get true random chaos.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-37e429aa32845eea152e7de9b762a690bcfe8830%252FRandomAlignment_demo3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=eb017d75&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#noise)

Noise

Direction based on the evaluation of a noise function at the placement's position.

Syntax: `**Noise**` or `**Noise(Noise:<noise>)**`

Abbreviation: `**N**` or `**N(N:<noise>)**`

The default `<noise>` is `Perlin(Freq:0.01)`.

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-2)

`//ezsc Clipboard Constant Noise`

*   Top-down screenshot
    
*   `<primary>` is still up and only the `<secondary>` is set to Noise.
    
*   The default Noise is Perlin Noise.
    

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-6499538aac3c70fa10e03caf47ab2878151fb62c%252FNoiseAlignment_example2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4a58dbe2&sv=2)

`//ezsc Clipboard Constant Noise(N:Vor(Freq:0.02,DistReturn:cell))`

*   Same scenario as above but using [Cellular Noise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voronoi_diagram#/media/File:Coloured_Voronoi_3D_slice.svg)
    .
    
*   You can recognize how each cell has its own random direction.
    

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-4daeeb9ffb8eefb83d0d42b86ddeb7d1f111e92e%252FNoiseAlignment_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=8c99332&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#aim)

Aim

Your player's aim direction.

Syntax: `**Aim**`

Abbreviation: `**A**`

Note: For brushes, `Constant(Direction:aim)` will use your player's aim direction at the time of brush binding, while `Aim` will use the player's aim direction during each brush act.

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-3)

`//ezsc Clipboard Aim Constant`

If we set the `<primary>` to `Aim` then the up direction of our structure, the green beam in our example, will align with our current player's aim direction.

My player model is included in the picture for reference. That's where I was looking when I executed the command. _The aim direction is visualized in F3+B with the thin blue line_

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-0ccce62f82d3c38b0f10549ea532fd568921f3f0%252FAimAlignment_demo1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=70d1b198&sv=2)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-e6ed2a43ff14b267ed967c0b3c7ce51d1db63a71%252FAimAlignment_demo2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=dbd0594f&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#upward)

Upward

The most upward perpendicular direction to your aim.

Syntax: `**Upward**`

Abbreviation: `**U**`

Diagram[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#diagram)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-4b1edf7e9b53792b4fca6e01200d7498dcae71d4%252FAlignments_aimVSupward.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fefa549b&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#playerrelative)

PlayerRelative

The direction from the placement's position towards the current player position.

Syntax: `**PlayerRelative**`

Abbreviation: `**P**`

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-4)

`//ezsc Clipboard PlayerRelative Constant`

If you set the `<primary>` to `PlayerRelative`, then each structure is placed such that its up direction is pointing towards your player position.

If you look closely, you can see my player model in the pictures. That's where I executed the command.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-d32db308c2d8cfcd97c88177535ec0205ed6d082%252FPlayerRelative_demo1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bb7fda19&sv=2)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-52c5e908cd159e20252fb7c0289936b06e0a5b1a%252FPlayerRelative_demo2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=62c96c5b&sv=2)

`//ezbr place Shape(S:Cone,P:diamond_block) PlayerRelative Constant -s 12,36,12`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-73672ea6bb6b276622b45cf1ee08ca690abb0ade%252FPlayerRelative_demo3.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5c45e65f&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#surfacenormal)

SurfaceNormal

The approximate surface-normal in the region of the placement's position.

Syntax: `**SurfaceNormal**`

Abbreviation: `**S**`

By [normal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Normal_(geometry))
 we mean the direction perpendicular to the terrain in question.

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-5)

`//ezbr place Shape(P:57,S:Cone) SurfaceNormal Constant -s 12,36,12`

You can see our ingame alignment visualizer dynamically orient itself depending on which part of the terrain you are looking at when you are holding the brush.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-d3efa157d5e0a31b68a33e16bf21d12678af1b6a%252FSurfaceNormal_demo1.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a40cef4d&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#viewdiff)

ViewDiff

Define a direction using two clicks. Exclusively for brushes.

Syntax: `**ViewDiff**`

Abbreviation: `**V**`

Each placement requires a right click and a left click. The first right click sets the placement position at the targeted block. Left-clicking somewhere else then defines a direction: From your first (right) click target position to your second (left) click.

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-6)

`//ezbr place Clipboard SurfaceNormal ViewDiff`

Here I set the primary to SurfaceNormal and control the secondary direction with a second click through the ViewDiff mode. Pay attention to my hand. You can see me alternating between right- and left-clicks. A right click sets the placement position, and a left click sets the ViewDiff direction. Our ingame alignment visualizer dynamically updates depending on your movement and your actions.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-d1c10e89dd71c5e47aa8b1bfa77de1d4f4de7007%252Foutput.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c2a549b5&sv=2)

`//ezbr place Shape(S:Torus(Thickness:0.4),P:57) PlayerRelative ViewDiff -s 20,20,30 -k x -c 90`

This torus shape required a few more parameters, so this example turned out a bit longer than usual. What's important to notice though is that the primary is set to PlayerRelative, meaning the top of the torus always faces the player, and the secondary is set to ViewDiff, meaning the final orientation is determined with a second click. Here, after each right-click, I alternate between left-clicking above and left/right from the placement position to create a linked chain.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-133925d0c9bff45c48cbc08385e1da3bff145763%252Foutput%2520%281%29.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=70a13c6f&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#expression)

Expression

Define a direction through an expression over each placement position.

Syntax: `**Expression(Expression:=<expression>,Space:<space>)**`

Abbreviation: `**E(E:=<expression>,S:<space>)**`

Mandatory Arguments:

*   `**Expression**` **(**`**E**`**)**: An expression defining a 3D vector for each position in space.
    
    *   Input variables are `x`, `y`, `z`.
        
    *   Output variables are `rx`, `ry`, `rz`.
        
    *   For each placement, the expression will evaluated with the according placement position and the result used for the placement's alignment.
        
    

Optional Arguments:

*   `**Space**` **(**`**S**`**)**: Defines the domain of the input variables.
    
    *   Defaults to `WORLD`.
        
    *   `WORLD`: the placement position. x, y, z, are in world coordinates
        
    *   `LOCAL`: When used in...
        
        *   ezplace: Always 0,0,0.
            
        *   ezscatter: Coordinates shifted such that the center of the region is 0,0,0.
            
        *   ezarray: x=y=0. z=0 at the start of the path, z=L at the end of the path, whereby L is the length of the path.
            
        
    *   `NORMALIZED`: When used in...
        
        *   ezplace: Always 0,0,0.
            
        *   ezscatter: Coordinates normalized to the region such that x,y,z ∈ \[-1,1\].
            
        *   ezarray: x=y=0. z=0 at the start of the path, z=1 at the end of the path.
            
        
    

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-7)

`//ezsc TS(P:##Grayscale,S:Fur,T:=y) C Ex(E:"=rx=z;rz=-x",S:N)`

*   `TS(P:##Grayscale,S:Fur,T:=y)` is a fur shape in a grayscale gradient.
    
*   `C`, the primary, using the default up direction.
    
*   `Ex(E:"=rx=z;rz=-x",S:N)` sets the secondary to (z,0,-x), whereby x,z are the normalized placement position coordinates.
    

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-8d7d2b3a7f2bd62d3a10c84ce5da7e8597cf42ff%252FAlignmentsExpression_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5e6fac39&sv=2)

`//ezar Sh(S:Fur,P:clay) C E(E:"=rx=sin(2*pi*z);rz=cos(2*pi*z)",S:N) -g -12`

This example shows how the z coordinate ranges from 0 to 1 along the path when using normalized mode.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-c213ac1413103b71a747251d6f8802db94066fda%252FAlignmentsExpression_example2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6fb5ab85&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#tangential)

Tangential

The direction tangential to the path. Exclusively for arrays.

Syntax: `**Tangential**`

Abbreviation: `**T**`

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-8)

`//ezarray Clipboard Tangential Constant -g 11 -o 2`

The _Tangential_ direction points tangential to the spline path at the position of the placement. If you set the primary to _Tangential_, the top of the shape is pointing along the spline like this.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-28d06a1438fe68a71841bb81e96cbd43985ee86d%252FTangentialAlignment_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=367b4bb0&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#orthogonal)

Orthogonal

The direction orthogonal to the path. Exclusively for arrays.

Syntax: `**Orthogonal**` or `**Orthogonal(Angle:<angle>)**`

Abbreviation: `**O**` or `**O(A:<angle>)**`

The angle, given in degrees, defines the initial direction of the orthogonal direction, whereby 0° and 360°, will face up, 90° and 270° face left and right, and 180° faces down (at the first part of the spline at least. It may twist further along if the normal mode is set to CONSISTENT, which is the default setting).

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-9)

`//ezarray Clipboard Orthogonal Constant`

The _Orthogonal_ direction points perpendicular to the spline path at the position of the placement. If you set the primary to _Orthogonal_, the top of the shape will point perpendicular to the spline path like this.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-6b60af89162824db39caaaf6af4f77716ebb3373%252FOrthogonalAlignment_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e9dbf048&sv=2)

Here's a GIF going through the `<angle>` parameter:

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-4dff07a6c6e47e4116d861ba2b6d9011c35ed032%252FStructuresAlignmentsOrthogonal_example.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=445a610&sv=2)

`//ezarray Clipboard Orthogonal Constant -n HORIZONTAL`

The [\-n flag](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/array-parameters#spline-orientation-n)
 has a direct influence on the orthogonal direction.

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-09ddde9fe383b38041a6fe9a6a981901b5f2d1d7%252FOrthogonalAlignment_example2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=838842d0&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#mixed)

Mixed

You may combine any number of any of the other Alignment modes using a weighted list:

Syntax: `<weight1>%<alignment1>,<weight2>%<alignment2>,...`

Alignment directions are scaled by the given weight and summed up together.

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-10)

` //ezsc Sh(P:clay,S:Cone)`` ` `**Constant**` ` ``-s 11,30,11 -n 1 `

(for reference)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-1d335d15841aa92a7560c747c5020d9f009ed585%252FAlignmentsExpression_example3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bb117a4&sv=2)

` //ezsc Sh(P:clay,S:Cone)`` ` `**10%C,10%R**` ` ``-s 11,30,11 -n 1 `

GIF going through

*   `10%Constant`
    
*   `10%Constant,1%Random`
    
*   `10%Constant,2%Random`
    
*   ...
    
*   `10%Constant,10%Random`
    

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-860e4bbe8bac82542124dbf4666e21d6849a281f%252FAlignmentsMixed_example1.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2ce85c3c&sv=2)

* * *

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#parameters)

Parameters


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The following flags adjust how Alignments are calculated.

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#snap-to-angles-j)

Snap to certain directions: `[-j <snapDirections>]`

This parameter allows you to restrict the chosen alignment direction to the specified subset. E.g. snapping to / only allowing cardinal direction, i.e. 90° rotations.

Available options:

*   `**MULTIPLES_90**`
    
    *   Only allows multiples of 90°, i.e. all axis-aligned directions.
        
    
*   `**MULTIPLES_45**`
    
    *   Only allows multiples of 45°, i.e. axis-aligned directions AND all perfect diagonals.
        
    
*   `**MULTIPLES_22_5**`
    
    *   Only allows multiples of 22.5°.
        
    
*   `**MULTIPLES_15**`
    
    *   Only allows multiples of 15°.
        
    
*   `**DIAGONALS_1_1**`
    
    *   Only allows axis-aligned directions, and perfect "1:1" diagonals.
        
    
*   `**DIAGONALS_2_1**`
    
    *   Only allows the `DIAGONALS_1_1` directions and any "2:1" diagonals.
        
    
*   `**DIAGONALS_3_1**`
    
    *   Only allows the `DIAGONALS_2_1` directions and any "3:1" diagonals.
        
    
*   `**DIAGONALS_4_1**`
    
    *   Only allows the `DIAGONALS_3_1` directions and any "4:1" diagonals.
        
    
*   `**DIAGONALS_5_1**`
    
    *   Only allows the `DIAGONALS_4_1` directions and any "5:1" diagonals.
        
    

Examples[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#examples-11)

`//ezbrush Cl Constant ViewDiff -j MULTIPLES_45`

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-448ca3a50f6382fbd49be8debb4e5ce9dd3282ea%252FAlignmentSnapToAngles_example.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=788ee318&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/placement/primary+secondary-alignment#perturb-secondary-x)

Perturb Secondary: \[-x\]

In our primary+secondary system, placement fails if both vectors are collinear (which simply means they are on the same line).

By enabling this flag ezEdits tries to circumvent that case by perturbing the secondary direction by a small amount.

* * *

---

# 2D Spline Shapes | ezEdits Wiki

The following `//ezsp` subcommands feature splines from predefined 2D shapes swept along the spline path.

* * *

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#syntax)

Syntax


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`**//ezspline 2d**` `**<shape>**` `**<pattern>**` [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

*   `**<shape>**` : The 2D shape defines the cross-section of the spline. Choose one from the list below.
    
*   `**<pattern>**`: Specifies the block(s) the spline is made out of, e.g. `clay`.
    

_The remaining arguments are outlined on the_ [_Common Parameters_](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters)
 _subpage._

* * *

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#list-of-less-than-shape-greater-than-s)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#circle)

` //ezspline 2d`` ` `Circle (Ci)``(``//ezspline basic``)`

Circle Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#circle-spline)

`**//ezsp 2d Circle**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a simple cylindrical spline along the spline path.

*   _Cylinder shape has no parameters._
    

`//ezsp basic` is an alias of `//ezsp 2d Circle`.

 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)

*   _Square shape has no parameters._

`**//ezsp 2d RoundedSquare**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#super-circle)

` //ezspline 2d`` ` `SuperCircle (SC)`

SuperCircle Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#supercircle-spline)

`**//ezsp 2d SuperCircle([**``**Exponent:<value>**``**])**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a spline with the given super-circle shape as the cross-section along the spline path.

*   `**[**``**Exponent:<value>**``**]**` (`**E**`) (Default: 2.0)
    
    *   Determines the shape.
        
        *   below 1 are stars, 1 is a diamond, 2 is a circle, and above 2 approaches a square shape
            
        
    *   See [https://www.desmos.com/calculator/vewqf5sc0x](https://www.desmos.com/calculator/vewqf5sc0x)
        
    

Example:

`//ezsp 2d SuperCircle(``Exponent:``**0.5**``) clay 15`

This GIF goes through running the above command with the following set of exponent values `0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 3.0, 99.0`:

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-467355ebc11c5587a59f6fa1b555ddb3489848e0%252FSplinesSuperCircle.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bda1b5d6&sv=2)

* * *

#### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#undefined-5)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-541cae58696aee310c27bda1db34950597d6a376%252FSplinesCirclesCircle.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f755318&sv=2)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#circles-circle)

` //ezspline 2d`` ` `CirclesCircle (CC)` (`//ezspline rope``)`

CirclesCircle Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#circlescircle-spline)

`**//ezsp 2d CirclesCircle([**``**Count:<value>**``**],[**``**Filled:<boolean>**``**])**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates multiple cylinder splines next to each other along the spline path.

*   `**[**``**Count:<value>**``**]**` (`**C**`) (Default: 3)
    
    *   Determines how many circles there are in the circle of circles. Must be between 1 and 12.
        
    
*   `**[**``**Filled:<boolean>**``**]**` (`**F**`) (Default: false)
    
    *   Determines whether the inside should be filled or not.
        
    

See [https://www.desmos.com/calculator/ht9tak6nri](https://www.desmos.com/calculator/ht9tak6nri)

Example:

`//ezsp 2d CC(``Count:``**1**``) clay 15`

The following GIF has been generated by just running the above command, and incrementing the Count parameter each time, from **1** up to **10** in this case:

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-541cae58696aee310c27bda1db34950597d6a376%252FSplinesCirclesCircle.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f755318&sv=2)

` //ezspline 2d CirclesCircle`` ` `**-t 90**` ` ``clay 10 `

The following spline can be generated using the above command, which is simply applying the [twist parameter](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
:

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-09c07b462d02b4682ee70478cb90674efb911f1d%252FSplinesRope.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ff89e7fa&sv=2)

Or by using `//ezspline rope clay 10`

`//ezspline rope` is an alias for `//ezspline 2d CirclesCircle` `**-t 90**`

* * *

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#polygon)

` //ezspline 2d`` ` `Polygon (Po)`

Polygon Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#polygon-spline)

`**//ezsp 2d Polygon([**``**Sides:<value>**``**])**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a polygon-shaped spline along the spline path.

*   `**[**``**Sides:<value>**``**]**` (`**S**`) (Default: 5):
    
    *   The number of sides of the polygon. 3 means triangle, 4 means square, 5 means pentagon, etc. Must be at least 3.
        
    *   See [https://www.desmos.com/calculator/eemibllcg8](https://www.desmos.com/calculator/eemibllcg8)
        
    

Example:

`//ezsp 2d Polygon(``Sides:``**3**``) clay 15`

The GIF has been generated by running the above command, and incrementing the count parameter each time, from 3 up to 8 in this case:

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-ece345fac7d9ed1e739afef1c05bde672c5b8308%252FSplinesPolygon.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=638d2773&sv=2)

* * *

#### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#undefined-7)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-03d0df174d8663586af279e49b89b85034cf2457%252FSplinesRectangle.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=810d96df&sv=2)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#rectangle)

` //ezspline 2d`` ` `Rectangle (Re)`

Rectangle Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#rectangle-spline)

`**//ezsp 2d Rectangle([**``**X1:<value>**``**],[**``**Y1:<value>**``**],[**``**X2:<value>**``**],[**``**Y2:<value>**``**])**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a rectangle-shaped spline along the spline path.

*   `**[**``**X1:<value>**``**]**` (Default: -1.0):
    
    *   Defines the x-position of the first corner of the rectangle. Between -1 and 1.
        
    
*   `**[**``**Y1:<value>**``**]**` (Default: -1.0):
    
    *   Defines the y-position of the first corner of the rectangle. Between -1 and 1.
        
    
*   `**[**``**X2:<value>**``**]**` (Default: 1.0):
    
    *   Defines the x-position of the second corner of the rectangle. Between -1 and 1.
        
    
*   `**[**``**Y2:<value>**``**]**` (Default: 1.0):
    
    *   Defines the y-position of the second corner of the rectangle. Between -1 and 1.
        
    

(`**!**`) We provide a neat little interactive plot, in which you can position your rectangle and see what values match up to it and vice-versa: [https://www.desmos.com/calculator/jqyaujpdsk](https://www.desmos.com/calculator/jqyaujpdsk)

Example:

*   The "Hi" from above has been generated by running the following set of commands:
    
    *   ` //ezsp 2d`` ` `Re(x1:``**-1.0**``,y1:``**-1.0**``,x2:``**-0.6**``,y2:``**1.0**``)` ` ``clay 12 `
        
        *   (The left column from the H)
            
        
    *   ` //ezsp 2d`` ` `Re(x1:``**-0.2**``,y1:``**-1.0**``,x2:``**0.2**``,y2:``**1.0**``)` ` ``clay 12 `
        
        *   (The left column from the H)
            
        
    *   ` //ezsp 2d`` ` `Re(x1:``**-1.0**``,y1:``**-0.2**``,x2:``**0.2**``,y2:``**0.2**``)` ` ``clay 12 `
        
        *   (The horizontal line from the H)
            
        
    *   ` //ezsp 2d`` ` `Re(x1:``**0.6**``,y1:``**-1.0**``,x2:``**1.0**``,y2:``**0.2**``)` ` ``clay 12 `
        
        *   (The column of the i)
            
        
    *   ` //ezsp 2d`` ` `Re(x1:``**0.6**``,y1:``**0.6**``,x2:``**1.0**``,y2:``**1.0**``)` ` ``clay 12 `
        
        *   (The dot of the i)
            
        
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#undefined-8)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-a4ee36524bf9d0a0c21904ca2c12026634d25dfc%252FSplinesStar.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fab91643&sv=2)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#star)

` //ezspline 2d`` ` `Star (St)`

Star Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#star-spline)

`**//ezsp 2d Star([**``**Sides:<value>**``**],[**``**Depth:<value>**``**])**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a star-shaped spline along the spline path.

*   `**[**``**Sides:<value>**``**]**` (`**S**`) (Default: 5):
    
    *   The number of sides of the polygon. 3 means triangle, 4 means square, 5 means pentagon, etc. Must be at least 3.
        
    
*   `**[**``**Depth:<value>**``**]**` (`**D**`) (Default: 0.5):
    
    *   Sets how deep the folds of the star cut towards the center. Between 0 and 1.
        
    *   0 imitates polygons,
        
    *   Values close to 1 lead to extremely thin spikes.
        
    
*   (`**!**`) See [https://www.desmos.com/calculator/gqclaezcxc](https://www.desmos.com/calculator/gqclaezcxc)
    

* * *

#### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#undefined-9)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-84278e14f9db1efe31e44da87384e46e104af850%252FSplinesFlower.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fa08029f&sv=2)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#flower)

` //ezspline 2d`` ` `Flower (Fl)`

Flower Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#flower-spline)

`**//ezsp 2d Flower([**``**Count:<value>**``**],[**``**Depth:<value>**``**])**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/2d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a flower-shaped spline along the spline path.

*   `**[**``**Count:<value>**``**]**` (`**S**`) (Default: 5):
    
    *   The number of petals of the flower.
        
    
*   `**[**``**Depth:<value>**``**]**` (`**D**`) (Default: 0.5):
    
    *   Sets how deep the folds in between two petals of the flower cut towards the center. Between 0 and 1.
        
    
*   (`**!**`) See [https://www.desmos.com/calculator/tah7yjltyr](https://www.desmos.com/calculator/tah7yjltyr)

# 3D Spline Shapes | ezEdits Wiki

This page covers the `//ezspline 3d` subcommand which feature 3D spline shapes embedded along the spline path.

* * *

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#syntax)

Syntax


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`**//ezspline 3d**` `**<shape>**` `**<pattern>**` [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-s <stretch>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#stretch-s-less-than-stretchfactor-greater-than)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

*   `**<shape>**` : Choose one from the list below.
    
*   `**<pattern>**`: Specifies the block(s) the spline is made out of, e.g. `clay`.
    

_The remaining arguments are outlined on the_ [_Common Parameters_](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters)
 _subpage._

* * *

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#list-of-less-than-shape-greater-than-s)

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-cbd90d0f2bfc34ad51137c9d83903f09adc5308d%252FSplinesBeads.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e13651c6&sv=2)

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#beads)

` //ezspline 3d`` ` `Beads (Be)`

Bead spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#bead-spline)

`**//ezsp 3d Beads**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-s <stretch>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#stretch-s-less-than-stretchfactor-greater-than)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a beads-shaped spline along the selected positions.

*   _Beads shape has no parameters._
    

**Example:**

` //ezsp 3d`` ` `Beads` ` ``clay 10 `

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-cbd90d0f2bfc34ad51137c9d83903f09adc5308d%252FSplinesBeads.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e13651c6&sv=2)

_This shape can also be achieved with the_ [_Rings_](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#ezspline-3d-rings)
 _shape using the following set of parameters:_ `_Rings(E:0,T:1,G:0,M:2,N:2)_`

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#cubes)

` //ezspline 3d`` ` `Cubes (Cu)`

Cubes Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#cubes-spline)

`**//ezsp 3d Cubes([**``**Gap:<value>**``**])**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-s <stretch>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#stretch-s-less-than-stretchfactor-greater-than)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a set of warped cubes along the selected positions.

*   `**[**``**Gap:<value>**``**]**` (`**G**`) (Default: 0.5):
    
    *   Sets the gap between cubes
        
    

(`**!**`) We provide an interactive 3D plot to play around with all parameters: [https://www.desmos.com/3d/xbmia9wiwo](https://www.desmos.com/3d/xbmia9wiwo)

**Examples:**

` //ezsp 3d`` ` `Cubes` ` ``clay 7 `

Default gap is 0.5

` //ezspline 3d`` ` `Braids (Br)`

Braids Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#braids-spline)

`**//ezsp 3d Braids([**``**Thickness:<value>**``**])**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-s <stretch>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#stretch-s-less-than-stretchfactor-greater-than)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a braids-shaped spline along the selected positions.

*   `**[**``**Thickness:<value>**``**]**` (`**T**`) (Default: 0.5):
    
    *   Sets the relative thickness of the individual braids
        
    

(`**!**`) We provide an interactive 3D plot to play around with all parameters: [https://www.desmos.com/3d/89xdz5xmsh](https://www.desmos.com/3d/89xdz5xmsh)

**Examples:**

### 

[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#chainlink)

` //ezspline 3d`` ` `Chainlink (Ch)`

Chain-Link Spline[](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#chain-link-spline)

`**//ezsp 3d Chainlink([**``**Extrusion:<value>**``**],[**``**Thickness:<value>**``**],[**``**Gap:<value>**``**],[**``**MajorExponent:<value>**``**],[**``**MinorExponent:<value>**``**],[**``**Place:<value>**``**])**` [`**<pattern>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/3d-spline-shapes#syntax)
 [`**<radii>**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#radii)
 [`**[-s <stretch>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#stretch-s-less-than-stretchfactor-greater-than)
 [`**[-t <angle>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#twist)
 [`**[-p <kbParameters>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#kb-parameters)
 [`**[-q <quality>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#quality)
 [`**[-n <normalMode>]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#normal-mode)
 [`**[-h]**`](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/commands/spline/common-parameters#help-page)

Generates a highly customisable chainlink-shaped spline along the selected positions.

*   `**[**``**Extrusion:<value>**``**]**` (`**E**`) (Default: 0.2):
    
    *   The amount to length to add for each individual link along the chain.
        
    
*   `**[**``**Thickness:<value>**``**]**` (`**T**`) (Default: 1.0):
    
    *   The inner/minor radius of each link.
        
    
*   `**[**``**Gap:<value>**``**]**` (`**G**`) (Default: 0.0):
    
    *   Amount to offset each link by, adjusting the overlap of the links in the chain.
        
    
*   `**[**``**MajorExponent:<value>**``**]**` (`**M**`) (Default: 3.0):
    
    *   The exponent defining the outer shape of an individual chain link.
        
    
*   `**[**``**MinorExponent:<value>**``**]**` (`**N**`) (Default: 3.0):
    
    *   The exponent defining the shape of the cross-section of an individual chain link.
        
    
*   `**[**``**Place:<value>**``**]**` (`**P**`) (Default: "BOTH"):
    
    *   Choose between "FIRST", "SECOND", or "BOTH" to place only half of the chain links or both.
        
    

(`**!**`) We provide an interactive 3D plot to play around with all parameters (it's very neat): [https://www.desmos.com/3d/yvrsv605mf](https://www.desmos.com/3d/yvrsv605mf)

**Examples:**

` //ezsp 3d`` ` `Chainlink` ` ``clay 10 `

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-bc7d69f736635e45676a111adfcc8a2c09ed7e16%252FSplinesChainlink_example1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fe26d682&sv=2)

` //ezsp 3d`` ` `Chainlink(M:99,N:99,Extrusion:0.6)` ` ``clay 10 `

*   `M:99` is responsible for making the chains appear rectangular (instead of elliptical).
    
*   `N:99` is responsible for making the square chain link's cross-section square-shaped.
    

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-e697f0e0e2d3dd6bd280b63e8a30fb8376b0ea0b%252FSplinesChainlink_example2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=909bc51b&sv=2)

` //ezsp 3d`` ` `Chainlink(M:1,N:1,E:0.7,G:-0.2,T:1.2)` ` ``clay 11 `

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-e7e21903a4afaa003fe0a4650c3201b102d93f54%252FSplinesChainlink_example3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9facf6b5&sv=2)

` //ezsp 3d`` ` `Chainlink(M:2,N:2,E:0,G:1)` ` ``clay 11 `

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-bf9000d7c197123acd34d050488127232ffe4fd0%252FSplinesChainlink_example4.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cdddba9d&sv=2)

` //ezspline 3d`` ` `Chainlink(P:FIRST)` `red_terracotta` ` ``10 `

` //ezspline 3d`` ` `Chainlink(P:SECOND)` `blue_wool` ` ``10 `

![](https://ezedits.gitbook.io/ezedits/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F62542430-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FmwyNbIIrWCkyIco2qJ9j%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-8999c43b537d57f21f4b69602fcdfb77a4ebd280%252FSplinesChainlink_example5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=285f3e1f&sv=2)
